SUr.iMARY OF THIE CC»!BINED METHOD 
FOR GLYCOL AND CARBINOL BSTB!ATION 

A 3 cc, sample of supernatant fermentation liquor is pipetted 
into a 100 cc. volumetric flask and made up to approximately 70 cc. 
with water. 5 cc. of a 20% solution of CuSO^ is added, followed by 
5 cc. of a 20% suspension of Ca(QH)2« The mixture is gently shaken 
and allowed to stand for 20 minutes after which it is made up to vol¬ 
ume. An aliquot of about 25 cc. is centrifuged. The remainder con- • 
tained in the volumetric flask is placed in a boiling water bath for 
15 minutes, cooled, and an aliquot centrifuged. Both aliquots are 
prepared for titration, the first one (no bath treatment) without any 
delay. 2 cc. of supernatant liquid are pipetted into a 125 x 35 ram. 
test tube follov;ed by 2 cc. of 1.0 N H2SO4, and 5 cc. of .01 M HIO^. 
This is allowed to stand at room temperature for approximately 15 
minutes. Then 10 cc. of 0.5 M NaHPO^, and 1 cc. of 30% KI and some 
starch indicator are added. 

The mixture is titrated immediately with 0.005 N Na2S202 to the 
disappearance of the blue color. 

A blank determination gives a titration of about 15.5 cc. 

Since 1 cc. of .005 N Na2S203 is equivalent to 0,225 gm. of 
glycol the calculation is as follows: 

(Blank titration minus sample titration in cc.) x 0.375 • % glycol. 

The same factor has been used in carbinol calculation, considering the 
difference obtained between bath treated and non-bath treated aliquots 
as carbinol. 

The above method was found to be reliable for fermentation liquors 
containing up to 4% sugar where only small amounts of carbinol are

present, and has been found reliable when at least 2 % sugar and

THE DBTSroaNATION OF REDUCING SUa\RS 


(Fran the Northern Regional Research Laboratory Methods) 


Principle 

The method is a modified Shaffer-Hartmann procedure* 


Reagents 

(a) N/lO potassium dichromate solution (4.001 gm. 
in 1 litre) 

(b) Starch indicator solution, 0.5% 

(c) Alkaline copper solution 
CuSO^.SHgO, 25 gra* per litre 

sodium citrate 5.5 H 2 O, 90 gm. per litre 
sodium carbonate (anhydrous) 50 gm. per litre 

Dissolve CuSO^ separately, pour slowly into solution of 

sodium salts v/ith stirring. 

(d) Iodide - iodate KI, 60 gm. per litre 

- KIO 3 - 5.4 gm. per litre 

Add 1 gn. of NaOH per litre to stabilize . 

(e) 5 N sulphuric acid solution (278 cc. cone. 
H 2 SO 4 per 2 litres) 

(f) Potassium oxalate solution (330 gm. ^2^2^4: 
per litre) 

(g) N/10 sodium thiosulphate solution (24, 82 gm. 
Na 2 S 203 . 5 H 20 per litre)

Add 2 gn. NaKCOj per litre . 

50 ml* of the alkaline copper reagent is pipetted into a 
300 ml* firlenmeyer flask. An aliquot of the solution to be 
tested containing 25 to 150 mgm, of sugar is added, together with 
distilled water to bring the total volume to 100 ml. The flask 
is placed on a hot plate adjusted in such a way as to bring the 
solution to boiling in 4 minutes. The flask is then boiled for 5 
minutes; during boiling small beakers are inverted over the flasks 
to prevent evaporation. The flasks are cooled in a water bath to 
at least 40 to 50^0* From a pipette exactly 25 ml. of KI -KIO 3 
solution is added, together with 20 ml, of 5 N H 2 SO 4 added care¬ 
fully, and 20 ml. of K 2 C 2 O 4 solution. The solution is well 
shaken and allowed to stand about half a minute until it is clear. 
It is then titrated with N/lO Na 2 S 203 using starch solution as 
indicator, A blank consisting of 50 ml. of alkaline copper 
reagent and 50 ml. of distilled water is analyzed at the same 
time. 

Calculation 

(Blank - thiosulphate titration) x 6.357 r mgm. of Cu. 

From a graph previously constructed the mgm of Cu can be 
read off as mgm. of sugar directly. 

Interfering substances 

Acetylmethylcarbinol is capable of reducing copper salts and 
makes the apparent glucose result too high. The correction factor 
is applied as follows; 

Apparent glucose minus acetylmethylcarbinol x 0.87) s true 

glucose

THS DETERMINA.TION OF REDUCING SUGARS 

IN MALT-HYDROLYZSD MEDIA 


(Reference A.O.A.C, - 5th Edition) 


Method 

Take a 5 cc. sample of the solution and add 85 cc. HgO 
and 10 cc. 2.0 N HCL or H 2 SO 4 . (This gives a 0.2 N HCL or 
H 2 SO 4 solution). Autoclave the acid mixture in an Erlenmeyer 
for J hour at 15 lbs. pressure. The maltose present will be 
completely hydrolyzed to dextrose. When cool add 0.1 N-NaOH 
until neutral to litmus. 

Detemine the reducing sugar by the modified Schaffer- 
Hartraann procedure. Report the results as percent dextrose. 

METHODS FOR DSTmilNING ETHYL AIOOHOL 

Distillation Method (from N.R.R.L. Methods) 


Apparatus 

A 500 ml. boiling flask; a Kjeldahl adapter with a 50 ml. 
separatory funnel connected to a coil condenser 15 inches long; 
a 200 ml. pressure bottle; a water bath. 

Reagents 


(a) 

0.2 N K 2 Cr 207 (9.801 gm. 

per litre) 

(b) 

0.2 N NaS203.H20 (49.638 

per litre) 

( 0 ) 

10 % potassium iodide 


(d) 

50% H 2 SO 4 . 


(e) 

Starch indicator

-5- 


The fermented mash is centrifuged and a 25 ml. sample of the 
supernatant liquor removed and placed in the 500 ml. boiling flask 
along with 1 ml. of 6N NaOH and 25 ml. of water. The stopper, 
fitted with Kjeldahl adapter and separatory funnel , is put in and 
connection made with a vertical coil condenser. The receiver is 
a 50 ml. volumetric flask. The contents of the flask are distilled 
at such a rate that about 30 ml. of the liquid comes over in 
20 to 25 minutes. At the same time water is run into the distill¬ 
ation flask at such a rate that there is no change in volume during 
the distillation. The receiving flask is made up accurately to 
50 ml. and analyzed directly or diluted if necessary. 

One ml. of the alcohol-containing distillate (with not more 
than 30 mgm. alcohol) is placed with 15 ml. of 0.2 W potassium 
dichromate and 20 ml. of 50% sulphuric acid in a 200 ml. well 
stoppered pressure bottle, which is well shaken and placed in a 
boiling water bath for 20 minutes. It is then cooled and diluted 
to 150 ml. with water, after which 10 ml. of 10% potassium iodide 
is added. The free iodine is titrated with 0.2N Na2S202, using 
starch as an indicator.

methylcarbinol and 2,3 butylene glycol are the only Interfering 
compounds. It has been found by experiment that the distillation 
method used for the recovery of the alcohol separates out almost 
all the butylene glycol and a large proportion of the acetylmethyl- 
carblnol. 

90 gm. butylene glycol ■ 6 litres normal thiosulphate 

88 gm. acetoln ■ 4 litres normal thiosulphate 

Corrections 

In routine tests the correction for butylene glycol Is 
negligible. For each 1^ acetylmethylcarbinol is the original 
fementation solution 0.014% must be subtracted from the final 
alcohol results.
